           <b>Ethnicity:</b> 
           <ul>
            <li>18.3% <a href="/wiki/Hispanic_and_Latino_Americans" title="Hispanic and Latino Americans">Hispanic or Latino</a></li> 
            <li>81.7% non-Hispanic or Latino</li>
           </ul> 
          </div></td>

      <p>The <b>United States of America</b> (<b>USA</b>) is a <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_state" title="Sovereign state">sovereign country</a> in <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">North America</a>. It is commonly called the <b>United States</b> (<b>U.S.</b>) or <b>America</b>. There are <a href="/wiki/Contiguous_United_States" title="Contiguous United States">forty-eight states</a> that border each other and <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">Washington, D.C.</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Capital_districts_and_territories" title="Capital districts and territories">capital district</a>. These states are between the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">Pacific</a> and <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Oceans</a>. They are <a href="/wiki/Borders_of_the_United_States" title="Borders of the United States">bordered</a> by <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a> to the north and <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a> to the south. The state of <a href="/wiki/Alaska" title="Alaska">Alaska</a> is in the northwest of the continent, with Canada to its east and <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a> to the west across the <a href="/wiki/Bering_Strait" title="Bering Strait">Bering Strait</a>. The state of <a href="/wiki/Hawaii" title="Hawaii">Hawaii</a> is an <a href="/wiki/Archipelago" title="Archipelago">archipelago</a> in the mid-Pacific. The country also possesses <a href="/wiki/Territories_of_the_United_States" title="Territories of the United States">some territories</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Insular_area" title="Insular area">insular areas</a>, in the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a> and Pacific. The city with the highest population is <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>. At 3.79 million square miles (9.83 million km<sup>2</sup>) and with about 331 million people, the United States is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_area" title="List of countries by area">third or fourth-largest</a> country by total area and the third-largest by land area and <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_and_dependencies_by_population" title="List of countries and dependencies by population">by population</a>. </p>
      <p>The United States is one of the world's most <a href="/w/index.php?title=Multiethnic_society&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Multiethnic society (not yet started)">ethnically mixed</a> and <a href="/wiki/Multiculturalism" title="Multiculturalism">multicultural</a> nations, the product of large-scale immigration from many countries.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[8]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_the_United_States" title="Economy of the United States">U.S. economy</a> is the largest national economy in the world, with an estimated 2016 <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">gross domestic product</a> (GDP) of <a href="/wiki/US$" class="mw-redirect" title="US$">US$</a>20.4 trillion (about a quarter of worldwide GDP).<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[9]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The nation was founded by <a href="/wiki/Thirteen_Colonies" title="Thirteen Colonies">thirteen colonies</a> of <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Great_Britain" title="Kingdom of Great Britain">Great Britain</a> along the <a href="/wiki/East_Coast_of_the_United_States" title="East Coast of the United States">Atlantic seaboard</a>. On July 4, 1776, they issued the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Declaration_of_Independence" title="United States Declaration of Independence">Declaration of Independence</a>, which announced their independence from Great Britain and their creation of a cooperative union. The disobedient states defeated Great Britain in the <a href="/wiki/American_Revolutionary_War" title="American Revolutionary War">American Revolutionary War</a>, the first successful <a href="/wiki/History_of_colonialism" title="History of colonialism">colonial war of independence</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[10]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Convention" class="mw-redirect" title="Philadelphia Convention">Philadelphia Convention</a> adopted the current <a href="/wiki/United_States_constitution" class="mw-redirect" title="United States constitution">United States Constitution</a> on September 17, 1787; its approval the following year made the states part of a single republic with a strong central government. The <a href="/wiki/Bill_of_Rights" class="mw-redirect" title="Bill of Rights">Bill of Rights</a>, making up ten <a href="/wiki/List_of_amendments_to_the_United_States_Constitution" title="List of amendments to the United States Constitution">constitutional amendments</a> guaranteeing many basic civil rights and freedoms, was approved in 1791. </p>
      <p>In the 19th century, the United States got land from <a href="/wiki/Louisiana_Purchase" title="Louisiana Purchase">France</a>, <a href="/wiki/Adams%E2%80%93On%C3%ADs_Treaty" title="Adams–Onís Treaty">Spain</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Oregon_Territory" title="Oregon Territory">United Kingdom</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mexican%E2%80%93American_War" title="Mexican–American War">Mexico</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Alaska_Purchase" title="Alaska Purchase">Russia</a>, and took over the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Texas" title="Republic of Texas">Republic of Texas</a> and the Republic of Hawaii. Arguments between the <a href="/wiki/Southern_United_States" title="Southern United States">farming-based South</a> and <a href="/wiki/Northern_United_States" title="Northern United States">industrial North</a> over the growth of the <a href="/wiki/Slavery_in_the_United_States" title="Slavery in the United States">institution of slavery</a> and <a href="/wiki/States%27_rights" title="States' rights">states' rights</a> began the <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">American Civil War</a> of the 1860s. The North's victory prevented a permanent split of the country and led to the <a href="/wiki/Thirteenth_Amendment_to_the_United_States_Constitution" title="Thirteenth Amendment to the United States Constitution">end of legal slavery</a> in the United States. By the 1870s, the national wealth was the world's largest.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[11]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Spanish%E2%80%93American_War" title="Spanish–American War">Spanish–American War</a> and <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a> confirmed the country's status as a military power. In 1945, the United States came out from <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a> as the <a href="/wiki/Atomic_bombings_of_Hiroshima_and_Nagasaki" title="Atomic bombings of Hiroshima and Nagasaki">first country with nuclear weapons</a>, a permanent member of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council" title="United Nations Security Council">United Nations Security Council</a>, and a founding member of <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a>. The end of the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Soviet_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="Dissolution of the Soviet Union">breaking up of the Soviet Union</a> left the United States as the only <a href="/wiki/Superpower" title="Superpower">superpower</a>. The country accounts for about half of worldwide military spending and is a leading economic, political, and cultural force in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[12]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div id="toc" class="toc" role="navigation" aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading">

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography_and_environment">Geography and environment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=1" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Geography and environment">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Change section: Geography and environment">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_the_United_States" title="Geography of the United States">Geography of the United States</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Climate_of_the_United_States&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Climate of the United States (not yet started)">Climate of the United States</a>, and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Environment_of_the_United_States&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Environment of the United States (not yet started)">Environment of the United States</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The United States is a <a href="/wiki/Federal_republic" title="Federal republic">federal republic</a> of fifty <a href="/wiki/U.S._state" title="U.S. state">states</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">federal district</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Territories_of_the_United_States" title="Territories of the United States">several territories</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[13]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[14]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[15]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The land area of the <a href="/wiki/Contiguous_United_States" title="Contiguous United States">contiguous United States</a> is 2,959,064 square miles (7,663,941&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup>). Alaska, separated from the contiguous United States by Canada, is the largest state at 663,268 square miles (1,717,856&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup>). Hawaii, occupying an archipelago in the central <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">Pacific</a>, southwest of North America, is 10,931 square miles (28,311&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup>) in area.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[16]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The United States is the world's third or fourth <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_area" title="List of countries by area">largest nation by total area</a> (land and water), ranking behind Russia and Canada and just above or below <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>. The ranking varies depending on how two territories disputed by China and <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a> are counted and how the total size of the United States is measured: calculations range from 3,676,486 square miles (9,522,055&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup>)<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[17]</a></sup> to 3,717,813 square miles (9,629,091&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup>)<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[18]</a></sup> to 3,794,101 square miles (9,826,676&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup>).<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[19]</a></sup> Measured by only land area, the United States is third in size behind Russia and China, just ahead of Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[20]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Haliaeetus_leucocephalus2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Haliaeetus_leucocephalus2.jpg/200px-Haliaeetus_leucocephalus2.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="250" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Haliaeetus_leucocephalus2.jpg/300px-Haliaeetus_leucocephalus2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Haliaeetus_leucocephalus2.jpg/400px-Haliaeetus_leucocephalus2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2562" data-file-height="3198"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Haliaeetus_leucocephalus2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Bald_Eagle" class="mw-redirect" title="Bald Eagle">Bald Eagle</a>, the national bird of the United States since 1782.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The coastal plain of the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic</a> seaboard gives way further inland to <a href="/wiki/Deciduous" title="Deciduous">deciduous</a> forests and the rolling hills of the Piedmont. The <a href="/wiki/Appalachian_Mountains" title="Appalachian Mountains">Appalachian Mountains</a> divide the eastern seaboard from the <a href="/wiki/Great_Lakes" title="Great Lakes">Great Lakes</a> and the grasslands of the <a href="/wiki/Midwestern_United_States" title="Midwestern United States">Midwest</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Mississippi_River" title="Mississippi River">Mississippi</a>–<a href="/wiki/Missouri_River" title="Missouri River">Missouri River</a>, the world's fourth longest river system, runs mainly north–south through the heart of the country. The flat, fertile <a href="/wiki/Prairie" title="Prairie">prairie</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Great_Plains" title="Great Plains">Great Plains</a> stretches to the west, interrupted by <a href="/w/index.php?title=U.S._Interior_Highlands&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="U.S. Interior Highlands (not yet started)">a highland region</a> in the southeast. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Rocky_Mountains" title="Rocky Mountains">Rocky Mountains</a>, at the western edge of the Great Plains, extend north to south across the country, reaching altitudes higher than 14,000&nbsp;feet (4,300&nbsp;m) in <a href="/wiki/Colorado" title="Colorado">Colorado</a>. Farther west are the rocky <a href="/wiki/Great_Basin" title="Great Basin">Great Basin</a> and deserts such as the Chihuahua and <a href="/wiki/Mojave_Desert" title="Mojave Desert">Mojave</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Nevada_(U.S.)" class="mw-redirect" title="Sierra Nevada (U.S.)">Sierra Nevada</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cascade_Range" title="Cascade Range">Cascade</a> mountain ranges run close to the <a href="/wiki/West_Coast_of_the_United_States" title="West Coast of the United States">Pacific coast</a>, both ranges reaching altitudes higher than 14,000 feet. </p>
      <p>The United States, with its large size and geographical variety, includes most climate types. To the east of the 100th meridian, the climate ranges from <a href="/wiki/Humid_continental_climate" title="Humid continental climate">humid continental</a> in the north to <a href="/wiki/Humid_subtropical_climate" title="Humid subtropical climate">humid subtropical</a> in the south. The southern tip of <a href="/wiki/Florida" title="Florida">Florida</a> is tropical, as is Hawaii. The Great Plains west of the 100th meridian are semi-dry. Much of the Western mountains are <a href="/wiki/Alpine_climate" title="Alpine climate">alpine</a>. The climate is dry in the Great Basin, desert in the Southwest, <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_climate" title="Mediterranean climate">Mediterranean</a> in <a href="/w/index.php?title=Coastal_California&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Coastal California (not yet started)">coastal California</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Oceanic_climate" title="Oceanic climate">oceanic</a> in coastal <a href="/wiki/Oregon" title="Oregon">Oregon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Washington_(state)" title="Washington (state)">Washington</a> and southern Alaska. Most of Alaska is subarctic or polar. Extreme weather is not unusual—the states bordering the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Mexico" title="Gulf of Mexico">Gulf of Mexico</a> are prone to <a href="/wiki/Hurricanes" class="mw-redirect" title="Hurricanes">hurricanes</a>, and most of the world's <a href="/wiki/Tornado" title="Tornado">tornadoes</a> happen within the country, mainly in the Midwest's <a href="/wiki/Tornado_Alley" title="Tornado Alley">Tornado Alley</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[21]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The U.S. ecology is considered "<a href="/w/index.php?title=Megadiverse_countries&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Megadiverse countries (not yet started)">megadiverse</a>": about 17,000 species of <a href="/wiki/Vascular_plants" class="mw-redirect" title="Vascular plants">vascular plants</a> occur in the contiguous United States and Alaska, and over 1,800 species of <a href="/wiki/Flowering_plant" title="Flowering plant">flowering plants</a> are found in Hawaii, few of which occur on the mainland.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[22]</a></sup> The United States is home to more than 400 mammal, 750 bird, and 500 reptile and amphibian species.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[23]</a></sup> About 91,000 insect species have been described.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[24]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/w/index.php?title=Endangered_Species_Act&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Endangered Species Act (not yet started)">Endangered Species Act</a> of 1973 protects threatened and endangered species and their habitats, which are monitored by the <a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Fish_and_Wildlife_Service&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="United States Fish and Wildlife Service (not yet started)">United States Fish and Wildlife Service</a>. There are fifty-eight <a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_areas_in_the_United_States_National_Park_System&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="List of areas in the United States National Park System (not yet started)">national parks</a> and hundreds of other federally managed parks, forests, and <a href="/wiki/Wilderness" title="Wilderness">wilderness</a> areas.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[25]</a></sup> Altogether, the government owns 28.8% of the country's land area.<sup id="cite_ref-FL_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FL-29">[26]</a></sup> Most of this is <a href="/wiki/Protected_area" title="Protected area">protected</a>, though some is leased for oil and gas drilling, mining, logging, or cattle ranching; 2.4% is used for military purposes.<sup id="cite_ref-FL_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FL-29">[26]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=2" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: History">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Change section: History">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_United_States" title="History of the United States">History of the United States</a>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Native_Americans_and_European_settlers">Native Americans and European settlers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=3" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Native Americans and European settlers">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Change section: Native Americans and European settlers">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Native_Americans_in_the_United_States" title="Native Americans in the United States">Native Americans in the United States</a>, <a href="/wiki/European_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="European colonization of the Americas">European colonization of the Americas</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Thirteen_Colonies" title="Thirteen Colonies">Thirteen Colonies</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Cliff_Palace_-_Mesa_Verde_National_Park_-_Colorado,_USA_-_30_July_2010.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Cliff_Palace_-_Mesa_Verde_National_Park_-_Colorado%2C_USA_-_30_July_2010.jpg/220px-Cliff_Palace_-_Mesa_Verde_National_Park_-_Colorado%2C_USA_-_30_July_2010.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Cliff_Palace_-_Mesa_Verde_National_Park_-_Colorado%2C_USA_-_30_July_2010.jpg/330px-Cliff_Palace_-_Mesa_Verde_National_Park_-_Colorado%2C_USA_-_30_July_2010.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Cliff_Palace_-_Mesa_Verde_National_Park_-_Colorado%2C_USA_-_30_July_2010.jpg/440px-Cliff_Palace_-_Mesa_Verde_National_Park_-_Colorado%2C_USA_-_30_July_2010.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2816" data-file-height="2112"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Cliff_Palace_-_Mesa_Verde_National_Park_-_Colorado,_USA_-_30_July_2010.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>An ancient palace built by the <a href="/wiki/Anasazi_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Anasazi people">Anasazi people</a> in <a href="/wiki/Mesa_Verde_National_Park" title="Mesa Verde National Park">Mesa Verde National Park</a>, a <a href="/wiki/UNESCO_World_Heritage_Site" class="mw-redirect" title="UNESCO World Heritage Site">UNESCO World Heritage Site</a> in <a href="/wiki/Colorado" title="Colorado">Colorado</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>It is believed that the <a href="/wiki/Native_Americans_in_the_United_States" title="Native Americans in the United States">indigenous peoples of the continental United States</a>, including the <a href="/wiki/Alaska_Natives" title="Alaska Natives">natives of Alaska</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Settlement_of_the_Americas&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Settlement of the Americas (not yet started)">moved in from Asia</a>. They began arriving twelve or forty thousand years ago, if not earlier.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[27]</a></sup> Some, such as the <a href="/wiki/Pre-Columbian_era" title="Pre-Columbian era">pre-Columbian</a> <a href="/wiki/Mississippian_culture" title="Mississippian culture">Mississippian culture</a> in the southeast, developed advanced farming, grand construction, and state-level communities. The <a href="/w/index.php?title=Population_history_of_indigenous_peoples_of_the_Americas&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Population history of indigenous peoples of the Americas (not yet started)">native population of America decreased</a> after <a href="https://simple.wiktionary.org/wiki/Europeans" class="extiw" title="wikt:Europeans">Europeans</a> arrived, and for different reasons, mostly sicknesses such as <a href="/wiki/Smallpox" title="Smallpox">smallpox</a> and <a href="/wiki/Measles" title="Measles">measles</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[28]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 1492, <a href="/wiki/Genoa" title="Genoa">Genoese</a> explorer <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Columbus" title="Christopher Columbus">Christopher Columbus</a>, under contract to the Spanish crown, reached some Caribbean islands, making the <a href="/w/index.php?title=First_contact_(anthropology)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="First contact (anthropology) (not yet started)">first contact</a> with the native people. On April 2, 1513, Spanish <a href="/wiki/Conquistador" title="Conquistador">conquistador</a> <a href="/wiki/Juan_Ponce_de_Le%C3%B3n" title="Juan Ponce de León">Juan Ponce de León</a> landed on what he called "<a href="/wiki/History_of_Florida" title="History of Florida">La Florida</a>"—the first recorded European coming on what would become the U.S. mainland. Spanish settlements in the area were followed by ones in the present-day <a href="/wiki/Southwestern_United_States" title="Southwestern United States">southwestern United States</a> that drew thousands through Mexico. French <a href="/wiki/Fur_trade" title="Fur trade">fur traders</a> established outposts of <a href="/wiki/New_France" title="New France">New France</a> around the <a href="/wiki/Great_Lakes" title="Great Lakes">Great Lakes</a>; France eventually claimed much of the North American interior, down to the Gulf of Mexico. The first successful English settlements were the <a href="/wiki/Colony_of_Virginia" title="Colony of Virginia">Colony of Virginia</a> in <a href="/wiki/Jamestown,_Virginia" title="Jamestown, Virginia">Jamestown</a> in 1607 and the <a href="/wiki/Pilgrim" class="mw-redirect" title="Pilgrim">Pilgrims</a>' <a href="/wiki/Plymouth_Colony" title="Plymouth Colony">Plymouth Colony</a> in 1620. The 1628 chartering of the <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts_Bay_Colony" title="Massachusetts Bay Colony">Massachusetts Bay Colony</a> resulted in a wave of relocation; by 1634, <a href="/wiki/New_England" title="New England">New England</a> had been settled by some 10,000 <a href="/wiki/Puritans" class="mw-redirect" title="Puritans">Puritans</a>. Between the late 1610s and the American Revolution, about 50,000 convicts were shipped to Britain's American colonies.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[29]</a></sup> Beginning in 1614, the Dutch settled along the lower <a href="/wiki/Hudson_River" title="Hudson River">Hudson River</a>, including <a href="/wiki/New_Amsterdam" title="New Amsterdam">New Amsterdam</a> on <a href="/wiki/Manhattan_Island" class="mw-redirect" title="Manhattan Island">Manhattan Island</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Independence_and_expansion">Independence and expansion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=4" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Independence and expansion">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Change section: Independence and expansion">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/American_Revolution" class="mw-redirect" title="American Revolution">American Revolution</a>, <a href="/wiki/American_Revolutionary_War" title="American Revolutionary War">American Revolutionary War</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Manifest_destiny" title="Manifest destiny">Manifest destiny</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Declaration_of_Independence_(1819),_by_John_Trumbull.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Declaration_of_Independence_%281819%29%2C_by_John_Trumbull.jpg/220px-Declaration_of_Independence_%281819%29%2C_by_John_Trumbull.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Declaration_of_Independence_%281819%29%2C_by_John_Trumbull.jpg/330px-Declaration_of_Independence_%281819%29%2C_by_John_Trumbull.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Declaration_of_Independence_%281819%29%2C_by_John_Trumbull.jpg/440px-Declaration_of_Independence_%281819%29%2C_by_John_Trumbull.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2976" data-file-height="1969"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Declaration_of_Independence_(1819),_by_John_Trumbull.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><i><a href="/w/index.php?title=Declaration_of_Independence_(Trumbull)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Declaration of Independence (Trumbull) (not yet started)">Declaration of Independence</a></i>, by <a href="/wiki/John_Trumbull" title="John Trumbull">John Trumbull</a>, 1817–18
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Tensions between American colonials and the British during the <a href="/wiki/American_Revolution" class="mw-redirect" title="American Revolution">rebel period</a> of the 1760s and early 1770s led to the <a href="/wiki/American_Revolutionary_War" title="American Revolutionary War">American Revolutionary War</a>, fought from 1775 through 1781. On June 14, 1775, the <a href="/wiki/Second_Continental_Congress" class="mw-redirect" title="Second Continental Congress">Continental Congress</a>, meeting in <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia" title="Philadelphia">Philadelphia</a>, established a <a href="/wiki/Continental_Army" title="Continental Army">Continental Army</a> under the command of <a href="/wiki/George_Washington" title="George Washington">George Washington</a>. Announcing that "<a href="/w/index.php?title=All_men_are_created_equal&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="All men are created equal (not yet started)">all men are created equal</a>" and are born with "certain <a href="/w/index.php?title=Natural_and_legal_rights&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Natural and legal rights (not yet started)">natural rights</a>," the Congress adopted the <a href="/wiki/Declaration_of_Independence" class="mw-redirect" title="Declaration of Independence">Declaration of Independence</a>, drafted mostly by <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Jefferson" title="Thomas Jefferson">Thomas Jefferson</a>, on July 4, 1776. That date is now celebrated every year as America's <a href="/wiki/Independence_Day_(United_States)" title="Independence Day (United States)">Independence Day</a>. In 1777, the <a href="/wiki/Articles_of_Confederation" title="Articles of Confederation">Articles of Confederation</a> established a weak federal government that operated until 1789. <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Morocco</a> became the first country in the world to recognise America’s independence.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[30]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>After the <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Yorktown" class="mw-redirect" title="Siege of Yorktown">British defeat</a> by American forces <a href="/w/index.php?title=France_in_the_American_Revolutionary_War&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="France in the American Revolutionary War (not yet started)">helped by the French</a>, Great Britain <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_(1783)" title="Treaty of Paris (1783)">recognized the independence of the United States</a> and the states' <a href="/wiki/Sovereignty" title="Sovereignty">sovereignty</a> over American land west to the <a href="/wiki/Mississippi_River" title="Mississippi River">Mississippi River</a>. A <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_Convention_(United_States)" title="Constitutional Convention (United States)">constitutional convention</a> was organized in 1787 by those wishing to establish a stronger national government, with powers of taxation. The <a href="/wiki/United_States_Constitution" class="mw-redirect" title="United States Constitution">United States Constitution</a> was approved in 1788, and the new republic's <a href="/wiki/1st_United_States_Congress" title="1st United States Congress">first Senate, House of Representatives</a>, and <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_States" title="President of the United States">President</a>—George Washington—took office in 1789. The <a href="/wiki/Bill_of_Rights" class="mw-redirect" title="Bill of Rights">Bill of Rights</a>, forbidding federal restriction of personal freedoms and certifying a range of legal protections, was adopted in 1791. </p>
      <p>Attitudes toward <a href="/wiki/Slavery_in_the_United_States" title="Slavery in the United States">slavery</a> were shifting; a <a href="/wiki/Article_One_of_the_United_States_Constitution#Section_9:_Limits_on_Congress" title="Article One of the United States Constitution">clause in the Constitution</a> protected the African slave trade only until 1808. The Northern states permanently stopped slavery between 1780 and 1804, leaving the <a href="/wiki/Slave_state" class="mw-redirect" title="Slave state">slave states</a> of the South as defenders of the "<a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Peculiar_Institution&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="The Peculiar Institution (not yet started)">peculiar institution</a>." The <a href="/wiki/Second_Great_Awakening" title="Second Great Awakening">Second Great Awakening</a>, beginning about 1800, made <a href="/wiki/Evangelicalism" title="Evangelicalism">evangelicalism</a> a force behind different social <a href="/w/index.php?title=Reform_movement&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Reform movement (not yet started)">reform movements</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Abolitionism" title="Abolitionism">abolitionism</a>. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:U.S._Territorial_Acquisitions.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/U.S._Territorial_Acquisitions.png/220px-U.S._Territorial_Acquisitions.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="149" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/U.S._Territorial_Acquisitions.png/330px-U.S._Territorial_Acquisitions.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/U.S._Territorial_Acquisitions.png/440px-U.S._Territorial_Acquisitions.png 2x" data-file-width="1536" data-file-height="1038"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:U.S._Territorial_Acquisitions.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Land-based purchases by date.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Americans' eagerness to <a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_territorial_acquisitions&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="United States territorial acquisitions (not yet started)">expand westward</a> caused a long series of <a href="/wiki/Indian_Wars" class="mw-redirect" title="Indian Wars">Indian Wars</a> and an <a href="/w/index.php?title=Indian_removal&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Indian removal (not yet started)">Indian removal</a> policy that stripped the native peoples of their land. The <a href="/wiki/Louisiana_Purchase" title="Louisiana Purchase">Louisiana Purchase</a> of French-claimed land under President Thomas Jefferson in 1803 almost doubled the nation's size. The <a href="/wiki/War_of_1812" title="War of 1812">War of 1812</a>, declared against Britain over different complaints and fought to a draw, strengthened U.S. <a href="/wiki/Nationalism" title="Nationalism">nationalism</a>. A series of U.S. military invasions into Florida led <a href="/wiki/Adams%E2%80%93On%C3%ADs_Treaty" title="Adams–Onís Treaty">Spain to give up</a> it and other Gulf Coast territory in 1819. The United States took over the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Texas" title="Republic of Texas">Republic of Texas</a> in 1845. The idea of <a href="/wiki/Manifest_destiny" title="Manifest destiny">Manifest destiny</a> became popular during this time.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[31]</a></sup> The 1846 <a href="/w/index.php?title=Oregon_Treaty&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Oregon Treaty (not yet started)">Oregon Treaty</a> with Britain led to U.S. control of the present-day <a href="/w/index.php?title=Northwestern_United_States&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Northwestern United States (not yet started)">American Northwest</a>. The U.S. victory in the <a href="/wiki/Mexican%E2%80%93American_War" title="Mexican–American War">Mexican–American War</a> resulted in the 1848 <a href="/wiki/Mexican_Cession" title="Mexican Cession">cession</a> of <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a> and much of the present-day <a href="/wiki/Southwestern_United_States" title="Southwestern United States">American Southwest</a>. The <a href="/wiki/California_Gold_Rush" title="California Gold Rush">California Gold Rush</a> of 1848–49 further encouraged western relocation. New railways made relocation easier for settlers and increased conflicts with Native Americans. Over a half-century, up to 40 million <a href="/wiki/American_bison" title="American bison">American bison</a>, or buffalo, were murdered for skins and meat and to ease the railways' spread. The loss of the buffalo, which were valuable to the <a href="/wiki/Plains_Indians" title="Plains Indians">plains Indians</a>, caused many native cultures to become gone forever. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Civil_War_and_industrialization">Civil War and industrialization</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=5" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Civil War and industrialization">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Change section: Civil War and industrialization">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">American Civil War</a>, <a href="/wiki/Reconstruction_era" title="Reconstruction era">Reconstruction era</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Spanish%E2%80%93American_War" title="Spanish–American War">Spanish–American War</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Battle_of_Gettysburg,_by_Currier_and_Ives.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Battle_of_Gettysburg%2C_by_Currier_and_Ives.png/220px-Battle_of_Gettysburg%2C_by_Currier_and_Ives.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="139" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Battle_of_Gettysburg%2C_by_Currier_and_Ives.png/330px-Battle_of_Gettysburg%2C_by_Currier_and_Ives.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Battle_of_Gettysburg%2C_by_Currier_and_Ives.png/440px-Battle_of_Gettysburg%2C_by_Currier_and_Ives.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="569"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Battle_of_Gettysburg,_by_Currier_and_Ives.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><i><a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Gettysburg" title="Battle of Gettysburg">Battle of Gettysburg</a></i>, lithograph by <a href="/w/index.php?title=Currier_and_Ives&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Currier and Ives (not yet started)">Currier and Ives</a>, ca. 1863
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/w/index.php?title=Origins_of_the_American_Civil_War&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Origins of the American Civil War (not yet started)">Tensions</a> between slave and <a href="/wiki/Slave_and_free_states" class="mw-redirect" title="Slave and free states">free states</a> mounted with arguments over the relationship between the <a href="/wiki/States%27_rights" title="States' rights">state and federal governments</a>, as well as <a href="/wiki/Bleeding_Kansas" title="Bleeding Kansas">violent conflicts</a> over the spread of slavery into new states. <a href="/wiki/Abraham_Lincoln" title="Abraham Lincoln">Abraham Lincoln</a>, a candidate of the mostly antislavery <a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="Republican Party (United States)">Republican Party</a>, was elected president in 1860. Before he took office, seven slave states declared their <a href="/wiki/Secession" title="Secession">secession</a>—which the federal government maintained was illegal—and formed the <a href="/wiki/Confederate_States_of_America" title="Confederate States of America">Confederate States of America</a>. With the Confederate <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Fort_Sumter" class="mw-redirect" title="Battle of Fort Sumter">attack upon Fort Sumter</a>, the <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">American Civil War</a> began and four more slave states joined the Confederacy. Lincoln's <a href="/wiki/Emancipation_Proclamation" title="Emancipation Proclamation">Emancipation Proclamation</a> committed the <a href="/wiki/Union_(American_Civil_War)" title="Union (American Civil War)">Union</a> to end slavery. Following the Union victory in 1865, three changes to the U.S. Constitution <a href="/wiki/Thirteenth_Amendment_to_the_United_States_Constitution" title="Thirteenth Amendment to the United States Constitution">secured freedom</a> for the nearly four million <a href="/wiki/African_Americans" title="African Americans">African Americans</a> who had been slaves,<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[32]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Fourteenth_Amendment_to_the_United_States_Constitution" title="Fourteenth Amendment to the United States Constitution">made them citizens</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Fifteenth_Amendment_to_the_United_States_Constitution" title="Fifteenth Amendment to the United States Constitution">gave them voting rights</a>. The war and its resolution led to a big increase in <a href="/wiki/Federalism_in_the_United_States" title="Federalism in the United States">federal power</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[33]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Ellis_island_1902.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Ellis_island_1902.jpg/220px-Ellis_island_1902.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="151" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Ellis_island_1902.jpg/330px-Ellis_island_1902.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Ellis_island_1902.jpg/440px-Ellis_island_1902.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1185" data-file-height="812"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Ellis_island_1902.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Immigrants landing on <a href="/wiki/Ellis_Island" title="Ellis Island">Ellis Island</a>, New York, 1902.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>After the war, the <a href="/wiki/Assassination_of_Abraham_Lincoln" title="Assassination of Abraham Lincoln">assassination of Abraham Lincoln</a> caused the <a href="/wiki/Reconstruction_era" title="Reconstruction era">Reconstruction</a>, where policies were put together directed at getting back and rebuilding the Southern states while securing the rights of the newly freed slaves. The resolution of the disputed <a href="/w/index.php?title=1876_United_States_presidential_election&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="1876 United States presidential election (not yet started)">1876 presidential election</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Compromise_of_1877" title="Compromise of 1877">Compromise of 1877</a> ended this era, and the <a href="/wiki/Jim_Crow_laws" title="Jim Crow laws">Jim Crow laws</a> soon <a href="/w/index.php?title=Disenfranchisement_after_the_Reconstruction_Era&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Disenfranchisement after the Reconstruction Era (not yet started)">disenfranchised many African Americans</a>. In the North, urbanization and a never-before-seen <a href="/w/index.php?title=Immigration_to_the_United_States&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Immigration to the United States (not yet started)">inflow of immigrants</a> from <a href="/wiki/Southern_Europe" title="Southern Europe">Southern</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Europe" title="Eastern Europe">Eastern Europe</a> made the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Technological_and_industrial_history_of_the_United_States&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Technological and industrial history of the United States (not yet started)">country's industrialization</a> grow rapidly. The wave of immigration, lasting until 1929, gave labor and changed American culture. High tax protections, national infrastructure building, and new banking laws encouraged growth also. The 1867 <a href="/wiki/Alaska_Purchase" title="Alaska Purchase">Alaska Purchase</a> from Russia completed the country's mainland expansion. The <a href="/wiki/Wounded_Knee_Massacre" title="Wounded Knee Massacre">Wounded Knee Massacre</a> in 1890 was the last major armed conflict of the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Wars" class="mw-redirect" title="Indian Wars">Indian Wars</a>. In 1893, the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Ancient_Hawaii&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Ancient Hawaii (not yet started)">native monarchy</a> of the Pacific <a href="/w/index.php?title=Hawaiian_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Hawaiian Kingdom (not yet started)">Kingdom of Hawaii</a> was ended in a secret and successful plan led by American residents; the United States took over the archipelago in 1898. Victory in the <a href="/wiki/Spanish%E2%80%93American_War" title="Spanish–American War">Spanish–American War</a> the same year proved that the United States was a <a href="/wiki/World_power" class="mw-redirect" title="World power">world power</a> and led to the addition of Puerto Rico, Guam, and the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a>. The Philippines gained independence fifty years later; Puerto Rico and Guam are still U.S. territories. </p> 
      <h3><span id="World_War_I.2C_Great_Depression.2C_and_World_War_II"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="World_War_I,_Great_Depression,_and_World_War_II">World War I, Great Depression, and World War II</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=6" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: World War I, Great Depression, and World War II">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Change section: World War I, Great Depression, and World War II">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Dust_Bowl_-_Dallas,_South_Dakota_1936.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Dust_Bowl_-_Dallas%2C_South_Dakota_1936.jpg/220px-Dust_Bowl_-_Dallas%2C_South_Dakota_1936.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Dust_Bowl_-_Dallas%2C_South_Dakota_1936.jpg/330px-Dust_Bowl_-_Dallas%2C_South_Dakota_1936.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Dust_Bowl_-_Dallas%2C_South_Dakota_1936.jpg/440px-Dust_Bowl_-_Dallas%2C_South_Dakota_1936.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2400" data-file-height="1800"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Dust_Bowl_-_Dallas,_South_Dakota_1936.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>An abandoned farm in <a href="/wiki/South_Dakota" title="South Dakota">South Dakota</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Dust_Bowl" title="Dust Bowl">Dust Bowl</a>, in 1936.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>As the <a href="/wiki/First_World_War" class="mw-redirect" title="First World War">First World War</a> erupted in Europe in 1914, the United States declared itself neutral. Afterward, the Americans sympathized with the British and French, even though many citizens, especially those from <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland" title="Republic of Ireland">Ireland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a>, were against the intervention.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[34]</a></sup> In 1917, they joined the <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_I" class="mw-redirect" title="Allies of World War I">Allies</a>, adding to the defeat of the <a href="/wiki/Central_Powers" title="Central Powers"><i>Central Powers</i></a>. Unwilling to participate in European affairs, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Senate" title="United States Senate">Senate</a> did not approve the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Versailles" title="Treaty of Versailles">Treaty of Versailles</a> (1919), which established the <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations" title="League of Nations">League of Nations</a>, applying a policy of unilateralism, which bordered on <a href="/w/index.php?title=Isolationism&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Isolationism (not yet started)">isolationism</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[35]</a></sup> In 1920, the <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_rights_movement" class="mw-redirect" title="Women's rights movement">Women's rights movement</a> gained the approval of a <a href="/wiki/Nineteenth_Amendment_to_the_United_States_Constitution" title="Nineteenth Amendment to the United States Constitution">constitutional amendment</a> to grant women the <a href="/wiki/Suffrage" title="Suffrage">right to vote</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[36]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>For most of the <a href="/wiki/1920s" title="1920s">1920s</a>, the country enjoyed a period of success, decreasing the inequality in the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Balance_of_payments&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Balance of payments (not yet started)">balance of payments</a> while profiting from industrial farms. This period, known as the <a href="/wiki/Roaring_Twenties" title="Roaring Twenties">Roaring Twenties</a>, ended with the <a href="/wiki/Wall_Street_Crash_of_1929" title="Wall Street Crash of 1929">Wall Street Crash of 1929</a> that triggered the <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression" title="Great Depression">Great Depression</a>. After his election as president in 1932, <a href="/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt" title="Franklin D. Roosevelt">Franklin D. Roosevelt</a> responded with the <a href="/wiki/New_Deal" title="New Deal">New Deal</a>, a series of policies that increased government interference in the economy.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[37]</a></sup> From 1920 to 1933 a prohibition <a href="/wiki/Prohibition_Era" title="Prohibition Era">banning alcohol</a> was in place.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[38]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Dust_Bowl" title="Dust Bowl">Dust Bowl</a> of the <a href="/wiki/1930s" title="1930s">1930s</a> left many poor farmer communities and encouraged a new wave of emigration to the West Coast.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[39]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Approaching_Omaha.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Approaching_Omaha.jpg/220px-Approaching_Omaha.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="157" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Approaching_Omaha.jpg/330px-Approaching_Omaha.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Approaching_Omaha.jpg/440px-Approaching_Omaha.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="2147"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Approaching_Omaha.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Soldiers of <a href="/wiki/United_States_Army" title="United States Army">United States Army</a> about to disembark on June 6, 1944 on <a href="/wiki/Omaha_Beach" class="mw-redirect" title="Omaha Beach">Omaha Beach</a> (France) during <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Normandy" class="mw-redirect" title="Battle of Normandy">Battle of Normandy</a> of <a href="/wiki/Second_World_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Second World War">Second World War</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The United States, officially neutral during the early stages of <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, began supplying supplies to the <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II" title="Allies of World War II">Allies</a> in March 1941, through the <a href="/wiki/Lend-Lease" title="Lend-Lease">Lend-Lease</a> program. On December 7, 1941, the country joined the Allies fight against the <a href="/wiki/Axis_Powers" class="mw-redirect" title="Axis Powers">Axis Powers</a>, after the <a href="/wiki/Attack_on_Pearl_Harbor" title="Attack on Pearl Harbor">Japanese attack on Pearl Harbor</a>. World War II boosted the economy by providing investment capital and jobs, making many women enter the labor market. Of the significant fighters, the United States was the only nation to be enriched by war.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[40]</a></sup> The discussions at <a href="/wiki/Bretton_Woods_system" title="Bretton Woods system">Bretton Woods</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yalta_Conference" title="Yalta Conference">Yalta</a> created a new system of international organization that placed the country and the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> at the heart of world affairs. In 1945, when the <a href="/w/index.php?title=End_of_World_War_II_in_Europe&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="End of World War II in Europe (not yet started)">end of the Second World War in Europe</a> came, an <a href="/w/index.php?title=United_Nations_Conference_on_International_Organization&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="United Nations Conference on International Organization (not yet started)">international gathering</a> held in <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco" title="San Francisco">San Francisco</a> drafted the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Charter_of_the_United_Nations&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Charter of the United Nations (not yet started)">Charter of the United Nations</a>, which came into force after the war.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[41]</a></sup> Having developed the <a href="/wiki/Manhattan_Project" title="Manhattan Project">first nuclear weapon</a>, the government decided to use it in the Japanese cities of <a href="/wiki/Atomic_bombings_of_Hiroshima_and_Nagasaki" title="Atomic bombings of Hiroshima and Nagasaki">Hiroshima and Nagasaki</a> in August of that same year. <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a> gave up on September 2, ending the war.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[42]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cold_War_and_civil_rights_era">Cold War and civil rights era</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=7" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Cold War and civil rights era">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Change section: Cold War and civil rights era">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a>, <a href="/wiki/McCarthyism" title="McCarthyism">McCarthyism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Civil_Rights_Movement" title="Civil Rights Movement">Civil Rights Movement</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vietnam_War" title="Vietnam War">Vietnam War</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Watergate_scandal" title="Watergate scandal">Watergate scandal</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Martin_Luther_King_-_March_on_Washington.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Martin_Luther_King_-_March_on_Washington.jpg/220px-Martin_Luther_King_-_March_on_Washington.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="238" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Martin_Luther_King_-_March_on_Washington.jpg/330px-Martin_Luther_King_-_March_on_Washington.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Martin_Luther_King_-_March_on_Washington.jpg/440px-Martin_Luther_King_-_March_on_Washington.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1296" data-file-height="1403"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Martin_Luther_King_-_March_on_Washington.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Martin_Luther_King,_Jr." class="mw-redirect" title="Martin Luther King, Jr.">Martin Luther King, Jr.</a> delivering his world-renowned "<a href="/wiki/I_Have_a_Dream" title="I Have a Dream">I Have a Dream</a>" speech in 1963.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Operation_Crossroads_Baker_Edit.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Operation_Crossroads_Baker_Edit.jpg/300px-Operation_Crossroads_Baker_Edit.jpg" decoding="async" width="300" height="157" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Operation_Crossroads_Baker_Edit.jpg/450px-Operation_Crossroads_Baker_Edit.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Operation_Crossroads_Baker_Edit.jpg/600px-Operation_Crossroads_Baker_Edit.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5137" data-file-height="2696"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Operation_Crossroads_Baker_Edit.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The "Baker" explosion, part of <a href="/w/index.php?title=Operation_Crossroads&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Operation Crossroads (not yet started)">Operation Crossroads</a>, at <a href="/w/index.php?title=Bikini_Atoll&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Bikini Atoll (not yet started)">Bikini Atoll</a>, Micronesia, in 1946.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a>, the United States and the Soviet Union competed after the Second World War, controlling the military affairs of Europe through <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Pact" title="Warsaw Pact">Warsaw Pact</a>. The first supported <a href="/wiki/Liberal_democracy" class="mw-redirect" title="Liberal democracy">liberal democracy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Capitalism" title="Capitalism">capitalism</a>, while the second favored communism and an economy <a href="/wiki/Planned_economy" class="mw-redirect" title="Planned economy">planned</a> by the government. Both supported several <a href="/wiki/Dictatorship" title="Dictatorship">dictatorships</a> and participated in <a href="/wiki/Proxy_war" title="Proxy war">proxy wars</a>. Between 1950 and 1953, U.S. troops fought <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Liberation_Army" title="People's Liberation Army">Chinese communist forces</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Korean_War" title="Korean War">Korean War</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-46">[43]</a></sup> From the break with the USSR and the start of the Cold War until 1957, <a href="/wiki/McCarthyism" title="McCarthyism">McCarthyism</a> also called the Second Red Dread, developed within the United States. The State unleashed a wave of political mistreatment and a campaign of prejudice against Communists, which some authors point out as of a <a href="/wiki/Totalitarianism" title="Totalitarianism">totalitarian</a> state. Hundreds of people were arrested, including celebrities, and between 10,000 and 12,000 people lost their jobs.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[44]</a></sup> The abuse ended when the courts declared it unconstitutional.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[45]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Nixon_leaving_whitehouse.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Nixon_leaving_whitehouse.jpg/220px-Nixon_leaving_whitehouse.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="250" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Nixon_leaving_whitehouse.jpg/330px-Nixon_leaving_whitehouse.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Nixon_leaving_whitehouse.jpg/440px-Nixon_leaving_whitehouse.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1063" data-file-height="1206"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Nixon_leaving_whitehouse.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Richard_Nixon" title="Richard Nixon">Richard Nixon</a> leaving the <a href="/wiki/White_House" title="White House">White House</a> after resigning as a result of the <a href="/wiki/Watergate_scandal" title="Watergate scandal">Watergate scandal</a>, August 9, 1974.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In 1961, the Soviet launch of the <a href="/wiki/Vostok_1" title="Vostok 1">first human-crewed spacecraft</a> caused President <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy" title="John F. Kennedy">John F. Kennedy</a> to propose to the country to be the first to send "<a href="/wiki/Apollo_program" title="Apollo program">a man to the Moon</a>", a fact completed in 1969.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[46]</a></sup> Kennedy also faced a tense <a href="/wiki/Cuban_Missile_Crisis" title="Cuban Missile Crisis">nuclear conflict</a> with the Soviet forces in <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a>, while the economy grew and expanded steadily. A growing <a href="/wiki/Civil_Rights_Movement" title="Civil Rights Movement">Civil Rights Movement</a>, represented and led by <a href="/wiki/African-Americans" class="mw-redirect" title="African-Americans">African-Americans</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Rosa_Parks" title="Rosa Parks">Rosa Parks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Martin_Luther_King,_Jr." class="mw-redirect" title="Martin Luther King, Jr.">Martin Luther King, Jr.</a> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=James_Bevel&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="James Bevel (not yet started)">James Bevel</a>, used nonviolence to deal with <a href="/wiki/Racial_segregation" title="Racial segregation">segregation</a> and <a href="/wiki/Discrimination" title="Discrimination">discrimination</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[47]</a></sup> After <a href="/wiki/Assassination_of_John_F._Kennedy" title="Assassination of John F. Kennedy">Kennedy's murder</a> in 1963, the <a href="/wiki/Civil_Rights_Act_of_1964" title="Civil Rights Act of 1964">Civil Rights Act of 1964</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Voting_Rights_Act_of_1965" title="Voting Rights Act of 1965">Voting Rights Act of 1965</a> were passed during the term of President <a href="/wiki/Lyndon_B._Johnson" title="Lyndon B. Johnson">Lyndon B. Johnson</a>. Johnson and his successor, <a href="/wiki/Richard_Nixon" title="Richard Nixon">Richard Nixon</a>, led a civil war in Southeast Asia, assistant to the unsuccessful <a href="/wiki/Vietnam_War" title="Vietnam War">Vietnam War</a>. A generalized <a href="/wiki/Counterculture" title="Counterculture">counterculture</a> movement grew, driven by <a href="/w/index.php?title=Opposition_to_United_States_involvement_in_the_Vietnam_War&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Opposition to United States involvement in the Vietnam War (not yet started)">opposition to war</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Black_nationalism&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Black nationalism (not yet started)">black nationalism</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Sexual_revolution" class="mw-redirect" title="Sexual revolution">sexual revolution</a>. A new wave of <a href="/wiki/Feminism" title="Feminism">feminist</a> movements also emerged, led by <a href="/wiki/Betty_Friedan" title="Betty Friedan">Betty Friedan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gloria_Steinem" title="Gloria Steinem">Gloria Steinem</a> and other women who sought political, social and economic equity. </p>
      <p>In 1974, as a result of the <a href="/wiki/Watergate_scandal" title="Watergate scandal">Watergate scandal</a>, Nixon became the first president to resign, to avoid being <a href="/wiki/Impeachment" title="Impeachment">dismissed</a> on charges such as obstruction of justice and abuse of power, and was succeeded by Vice President <a href="/wiki/Gerald_Ford" title="Gerald Ford">Gerald Ford</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[48]</a></sup> The presidency of <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Carter" title="Jimmy Carter">Jimmy Carter</a> in the 1970s was marked by <a href="/wiki/Stagflation" title="Stagflation">stagflation</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Iran_hostage_crisis" title="Iran hostage crisis">hostage crisis in Iran</a>. The election of <a href="/wiki/Ronald_Reagan" title="Ronald Reagan">Ronald Reagan</a> as president in 1980 announced a <a href="/wiki/Conservatism_in_the_United_States" class="mw-redirect" title="Conservatism in the United States">change in U.S. policy</a>, which was reflected in significant changes in <a href="/wiki/Reaganomics" title="Reaganomics">taxes and fiscal expenses</a>. His second term brought with it the <a href="/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Contra_affair" title="Iran–Contra affair">Iran–Contra affair</a> and the significant diplomatic progress with the Soviet Union. The later Soviet collapse ended the Cold War. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Modern_history">Modern history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=8" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Modern history">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Change section: Modern history">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/September_11_attacks" title="September 11 attacks">September 11 attacks</a>, <a href="/wiki/War_in_Afghanistan_(2001%E2%80%93present)" title="War in Afghanistan (2001–present)">War in Afghanistan (2001–present)</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iraq_War" title="Iraq War">Iraq War</a>, <a href="/wiki/Great_Recession" title="Great Recession">Great Recession</a>, and <a href="/w/index.php?title=International_military_intervention_against_ISIL&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="International military intervention against ISIL (not yet started)">International military intervention against ISIL</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:September_11_2001_just_collapsed.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/September_11_2001_just_collapsed.jpg/180px-September_11_2001_just_collapsed.jpg" decoding="async" width="180" height="271" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/September_11_2001_just_collapsed.jpg/270px-September_11_2001_just_collapsed.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/September_11_2001_just_collapsed.jpg/360px-September_11_2001_just_collapsed.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1152" data-file-height="1733"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:September_11_2001_just_collapsed.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A large cloud of dust surrounds the city of New York after the collapse of the Twin Towers after the terrorist attack of September 11, 2001.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Under President <a href="/wiki/George_H._W._Bush" title="George H. W. Bush">George H. W. Bush</a>, the country took on a global dominant role worldwide, as in the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_War" title="Gulf War">Gulf War</a> (1991). The longest economic expansion in modern American history, from March 1991 to March 2001, spanned the presidency of <a href="/wiki/Bill_Clinton" title="Bill Clinton">Bill Clinton</a> and the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Dot-com_bubble&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Dot-com bubble (not yet started)">dot-com bubble</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[49]</a></sup> A civil lawsuit and a <a href="/wiki/Monica_Lewinsky" title="Monica Lewinsky">sex scandal</a> led to his <a href="/wiki/Impeachment" title="Impeachment">impeachment</a> in 1998, although he managed to finish his period. The <a href="/wiki/2000_United_States_presidential_election" title="2000 United States presidential election">2000 presidential elections</a>, one of the most competitive in American history, they were settled by the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_the_United_States" title="Supreme Court of the United States">Supreme Court</a>: <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">George W. Bush</a>, son of George H. W. Bush, became president, even though he gained fewer votes than his opponent <a href="/wiki/Al_Gore" title="Al Gore">Al Gore</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[50]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On September 11, 2001, the terrorists of the <a href="/wiki/Al-Qaeda" title="Al-Qaeda">Al-Qaeda</a> group attacked the twin towers of the <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Center_(1973%E2%80%932001)" title="World Trade Center (1973–2001)">World Trade Center</a> in <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a> (which were destroyed) and <a href="/wiki/The_Pentagon" title="The Pentagon">the Pentagon</a> near <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">Washington, D.C.</a>, in a series of attacks that ended the life of nearly three thousand people. In response, the Bush administration launched the "<a href="/wiki/War_on_Terror" class="mw-redirect" title="War on Terror">War on Terror</a>." At the end of 2001, U.S. forces <a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_invasion_of_Afghanistan&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="United States invasion of Afghanistan (not yet started)">invaded Afghanistan</a>, toppled the <a href="/wiki/Taliban" title="Taliban">Taliban</a> government and destroyed Al-Qaeda's training camps. Taliban insurgents continue to fight a <a href="/wiki/Guerrilla_war" class="mw-redirect" title="Guerrilla war">guerrilla war</a>. In 2002, Bush began to push for a regime change to take place in <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[51]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[52]</a></sup> With NATO's lack of support and without a clear UN order for military intervention, Bush organized the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Coalition_of_the_willing&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Coalition of the willing (not yet started)">coalition of the willing</a>; The coalition forces quickly <a href="/wiki/2003_invasion_of_Iraq" title="2003 invasion of Iraq">invaded Iraq</a> in 2003 and toppled the statue of dictator <a href="/wiki/Saddam_Hussein" title="Saddam Hussein">Saddam Hussein</a>. The following year, Bush was re-elected as the most voted president in an <a href="/wiki/2004_United_States_presidential_election" title="2004 United States presidential election">election</a>. </p>
      <p>In 2005, <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Katrina" title="Hurricane Katrina">Hurricane Katrina</a>, which would end up being the deadliest natural disaster in national history, caused severe destruction along the Gulf Coast: the city of <a href="/wiki/New_Orleans" title="New Orleans">New Orleans</a> was devastated, with 1833 dead.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[53]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:ObamaTrump.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/ObamaTrump.jpg/170px-ObamaTrump.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="282" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/ObamaTrump.jpg/255px-ObamaTrump.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/ObamaTrump.jpg/340px-ObamaTrump.jpg 2x" data-file-width="413" data-file-height="686"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:ObamaTrump.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>President <a href="/wiki/Donald_Trump" title="Donald Trump">Donald Trump</a> with his predecessor <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a>, the first African American president.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>On November 4, 2008, during a <a href="/wiki/Great_Recession" title="Great Recession">global economic downturn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> was elected president, having been the first African American to take office. In May 2011, American Special forces managed to kill <a href="/wiki/Osama_bin_Laden" title="Osama bin Laden">Osama bin Laden</a>, hiding in Pakistan. The following year, Barack Obama was re-elected. Under his second term, he led the <a href="/w/index.php?title=International_military_intervention_against_ISIL&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="International military intervention against ISIL (not yet started)">war against the Islamic State</a> and restored diplomatic relations with Cuba. </p>
      <p>On November 8, 2016, the <a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="Republican Party (United States)">Republican Party</a> leader <a href="/wiki/Donald_Trump" title="Donald Trump">Donald Trump</a> defeated former First Lady <a href="/wiki/Hillary_Clinton" title="Hillary Clinton">Hillary Clinton</a> for presidency in an unusual election and whose plans have been described by political analysts as populist, protectionist and nationalist, assuming office on January 20, 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[54]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The massacres in <a href="/wiki/Orlando_nightclub_shooting" title="Orlando nightclub shooting">Orlando</a> of June 12, 2016 at the gay disco <i>Pulse</i> (51 dead) and in <a href="/wiki/2017_Las_Vegas_shooting" title="2017 Las Vegas shooting">Las Vegas</a> on October 1, 2017 (60) are listed as the largest massacres in the country since 9/11.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[55]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government">Government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=9" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Government">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Change section: Government">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Federal_government_of_the_United_States" title="Federal government of the United States">Federal government of the United States</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The United States is the world's oldest surviving <a href="/wiki/Federation" title="Federation">federation</a>. It is a <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_republic" title="Constitutional republic">constitutional republic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Representative_democracy" class="mw-redirect" title="Representative democracy">representative democracy</a>, "in which <a href="/wiki/Majority_rule" title="Majority rule">majority rule</a> is tempered by <a href="/wiki/Minority_rights" title="Minority rights">minority rights</a> protected by <a href="/wiki/Law_of_the_United_States" title="Law of the United States">law</a>."<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[56]</a></sup> The government is controlled by a system of <a href="/wiki/Separation_of_powers" title="Separation of powers">checks and balances</a> from the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Constitution" class="mw-redirect" title="United States Constitution">United States Constitution</a>. The constitution is the country's main legal <a href="/wiki/Document" title="Document">document</a>. There are three branches. They are the <i><a href="/wiki/Executive_branch" class="mw-redirect" title="Executive branch">executive branch</a></i>, the <i><a href="/wiki/Legislative_branch" class="mw-redirect" title="Legislative branch">legislative branch</a></i>, and the <i><a href="/wiki/Judicial_branch" class="mw-redirect" title="Judicial branch">judicial branch</a></i>. State governments and the federal government work in very similar ways. Each state has its own executive, legislative, and judicial branches. The executive branch of a state government is led by a <a href="/wiki/Governor" title="Governor">governor</a>, instead of a president. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Executive_branch">Executive branch</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=10" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Executive branch">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Change section: Executive branch">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Executive_branch" class="mw-redirect" title="Executive branch">executive branch</a> is the part of the government that enforces the law. Members of the <a href="/wiki/U.S._Electoral_College" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. Electoral College">U.S. Electoral College</a> elect a <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_States" title="President of the United States">president</a> who is the leader of the executive branch, as well as the leader of the <a href="/wiki/Armed_forces" class="mw-redirect" title="Armed forces">armed forces</a>. The president may <a href="/wiki/Veto" title="Veto">veto</a> a bill that the Congress has passed, so it does not become a law. The President may also make "executive orders" to ensure that people follow the law. </p>
