      <p>The president is in charge of many departments that control much of the day-to-day actions of government. For example, <a href="/wiki/Department_of_Commerce" class="mw-redirect" title="Department of Commerce">Department of Commerce</a> makes rules about trade. The president chooses the heads of these departments, and also nominates federal judges. However, the <a href="/wiki/Senate" title="Senate">Senate</a>, part of the legislative branch, must agree with all of the people the president chooses. The president may serve two 4-year terms. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Legislative_branch">Legislative branch</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=11" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Legislative branch">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Change section: Legislative branch">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:USCapitol.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/USCapitol.jpg/220px-USCapitol.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/USCapitol.jpg/330px-USCapitol.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/USCapitol.jpg/440px-USCapitol.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="600"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:USCapitol.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The west side of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Capitol" title="United States Capitol">United States Capitol</a>, which is home to the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Congress" title="United States Congress">United States Congress</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Legislative_branch" class="mw-redirect" title="Legislative branch">legislative branch</a> makes laws. The legislative branch is called the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Congress" title="United States Congress">United States Congress</a>. Congress is divided into two "houses". </p>
      <p>One house is the <a href="/wiki/United_States_House_of_Representatives" title="United States House of Representatives">House of Representatives</a>. The Representatives are each elected by voters from a set area within a state. The number of Representatives a state has is based on how many people live there. Representatives serve two-year terms. The total number of representatives today is 435. The leader of the House of Representatives is the <a href="/wiki/Speaker_of_the_House" class="mw-redirect" title="Speaker of the House">Speaker of the House</a>. </p>
      <p>The other house is the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Senate" title="United States Senate">Senate</a>. In the Senate, each state is represented equally, by two senators. Because there are 50 states, there are 100 senators. The President's <a href="/wiki/Treaty" title="Treaty">treaties</a> or appointments of <a href="/wiki/Official" title="Official">officials</a> need the Senate's approval. Senators serve six-year terms. The Vice President of the United States serves as president of the Senate. In practice, the vice president is usually absent from the Senate, and a senator serves as president <a href="/wiki/Pro_tempore" title="Pro tempore">pro tempore</a>, or <a href="https://simple.wiktionary.org/wiki/temporary" class="extiw" title="wikt:temporary">temporary</a> president, of the Senate. </p>
      <p>Representatives and senators <a href="/wiki/Proposal" title="Proposal">propose</a> laws, called "<a href="/wiki/Bill_(law)" class="mw-redirect" title="Bill (law)">bills</a>", in their respective houses. A bill may be voted upon by the entire house right away or may first go to a small group, known as a <a href="/wiki/Committees_of_the_United_States_Senate" title="Committees of the United States Senate">committee</a>, which may recommend a bill for a vote by the whole house. If one house votes to pass a bill, the bill then gets sent to the other house; if both houses vote for it, it is then sent to the president, who may sign the bill into law or <a href="/wiki/Veto" title="Veto">veto</a> it. If the president vetoes the bill, it is sent back to Congress. If Congress votes again and passes the bill with at least a two-thirds <a href="/wiki/Majority" title="Majority">majority</a>, the bill becomes law and cannot be vetoed by the president. </p>
      <p>Under the American system of <a href="/wiki/Federalism" title="Federalism">federalism</a>, Congress may not make laws that directly control the states; instead, Congress may use the promise of federal funds, or special circumstances such as national <a href="/wiki/Emergency" title="Emergency">emergencies</a>, to encourage the states to follow federal law. This system is both complex and unique. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Judicial_branch">Judicial branch</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=12" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Judicial branch">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Change section: Judicial branch">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Judicial_branch" class="mw-redirect" title="Judicial branch">judicial branch</a> is the part of government that interprets what the law means. The Judicial Branch is made up of the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_the_United_States" title="Supreme Court of the United States">Supreme Court</a> and many lower courts. If the Supreme Court decides that a law is not allowed by <a href="/wiki/Constitution" title="Constitution">the Constitution</a>, the law is said to be "struck down" and is no longer a <a href="/wiki/Validity" title="Validity">valid</a> law. </p>
      <p>The Supreme Court is made up of nine <a href="/wiki/Judge" title="Judge">judges</a>, called justices, who are nominated by the President and confirmed by the Senate. One of these justices, called the <a href="/wiki/Chief_Justice_of_the_United_States" title="Chief Justice of the United States">chief justice</a>, heads the court. A Supreme Court justice serves until he or she dies or <a href="/wiki/Resignation" title="Resignation">resigns</a> (quits in the middle of his or her term). When that happens, the president nominates someone new to replace the justice who left. If the Senate agrees with that choice, the person becomes a justice. If the Senate does not agree with the president's choice, then the president must nominate someone else. </p>
      <p>Famous court cases such as <i><a href="/wiki/Marbury_v._Madison" title="Marbury v. Madison">Marbury v Madison</a></i> (which was decided in 1803) have firmly established that the Supreme Court is the <a href="/wiki/Interpreter" title="Interpreter">ultimate interpreter</a> of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Constitution" class="mw-redirect" title="United States Constitution">United States Constitution</a> and has the power to strike down any law that <a href="/wiki/Conflict" title="Conflict">conflicts</a> with it.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[57]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=13" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Politics">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Change section: Politics">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/States_of_the_United_States" class="mw-redirect" title="States of the United States">States of the United States</a> and <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_the_United_States" title="Politics of the United States">Politics of the United States</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Political_System_of_the_United_States.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Political_System_of_the_United_States.svg/220px-Political_System_of_the_United_States.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="154" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Political_System_of_the_United_States.svg/330px-Political_System_of_the_United_States.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Political_System_of_the_United_States.svg/440px-Political_System_of_the_United_States.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="721" data-file-height="506"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Political_System_of_the_United_States.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The political system of the United States
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The United States of America consists of <a href="/wiki/States_of_the_United_States" class="mw-redirect" title="States of the United States">50 states</a>, 5 territories and 1 district (<a href="/wiki/Washington_D.C" class="mw-redirect" title="Washington D.C">Washington D.C</a>.). States can make laws about things inside the state, but federal law is about things dealing with more than one state or dealing with other countries. In some areas, if the federal government makes laws that say different things from the state laws, people must follow the federal law because the state law is not a law any more. Each state has a constitution of its own, different from the federal (national) Constitution. Each of these is like the federal Constitution because they say how each state's government is set up, but some also talk about specific laws. </p>
      <p>The federal and most state governments are dominated by two <a href="/wiki/Political_party" title="Political party">political parties</a>: the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Republican_Party" class="mw-redirect" title="United States Republican Party">Republicans</a> and the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Democratic_Party" class="mw-redirect" title="United States Democratic Party">Democrats</a>. There are many smaller parties; the largest of these are the <a href="/wiki/Libertarian_Party_(United_States)" title="Libertarian Party (United States)">Libertarian Party</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Green_Party_(United_States)" class="mw-redirect" title="Green Party (United States)">Green Party</a>. People help in political <a href="/wiki/Campaign" title="Campaign">campaigns</a> that they like. They try to persuade politicians to help them; this is called <a href="/wiki/Lobbying" title="Lobbying">lobbying</a>. All Americans are allowed to do these things, but some have and spend more money than others, or in other ways do more in politics. Some people think this is a problem, and lobby for rules to be made to change it. </p>
      <p>Since 2017, the president is a Republican, and Congress is also Republican-controlled, so the Republicans have more power in the federal government. There are still many powerful Democrats who can try to stop the Republicans from doing things that they believe will be bad for the country. Also, members of a party in power do not always agree on what to do. If enough people decide to vote against Republicans in the next election, they will lose power. In a republic like the United States, no party can do whatever they want. All politicians have to argue, compromise, and make deals with each other to get things done. They have to answer to the people and take responsibility for their mistakes. </p>
      <p>The USA's large <a href="/wiki/Culture" title="Culture">cultural</a>, economic, and military influence has made the <a href="/wiki/Foreign_policy_of_the_United_States" title="Foreign policy of the United States">foreign policy of the United States</a>, or relations with other countries, a topic in American politics, and the politics of many other countries. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_divisions">Political divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=14" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Political divisions">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Change section: Political divisions">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/U.S._state" title="U.S. state">U.S. state</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Territorial_evolution_of_the_United_States&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Territorial evolution of the United States (not yet started)">Territorial evolution of the United States</a>, and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Territorial_changes_of_the_United_States&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Territorial changes of the United States (not yet started)">Territorial changes of the United States</a>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="States">States</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=15" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: States">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Change section: States">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._states" title="List of U.S. states">List of U.S. states</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The United States <a href="/w/index.php?title=Military_conquest&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Military conquest (not yet started)">conquered</a> and <a href="/wiki/Purchase" title="Purchase">bought</a> new lands over time, and grew from the original 13 colonies in the east to the current 50 states, of which 48 of them are <a href="/wiki/Contigny" title="Contigny">joined together</a> to make up the <a href="/wiki/Continental_United_States" title="Continental United States">contiguous United States</a>. These states, called the "lower 48", can all be reached by <a href="/wiki/Road" title="Road">road</a> without crossing a <a href="/wiki/Border" title="Border">border</a> into another country. They go from the Atlantic east to the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Coast" class="mw-redirect" title="Pacific Coast">Pacific</a> in the west. There are two other states which are not joined to the lower 48 states. <a href="/wiki/Alaska" title="Alaska">Alaska</a> can be reached by passing through <a href="/wiki/British_Columbia" title="British Columbia">British Columbia</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Yukon" title="Yukon">Yukon</a>, both of which are part of Canada. <a href="/wiki/Hawaii" title="Hawaii">Hawaii</a> is in the middle of the Pacific Ocean. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">Washington, D.C.</a>, the national capital, is a <a href="/wiki/Federal_district" title="Federal district">federal district</a> that was split from the states of <a href="/wiki/Maryland" title="Maryland">Maryland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Virginia" title="Virginia">Virginia</a> in 1791. Not part of any US state, it used to be in the shape of a <a href="/wiki/Square" title="Square">square</a>, with the land west of the <a href="/wiki/Potomac_River" title="Potomac River">Potomac River</a> coming from Virginia, and the land east of the river coming from Maryland. In 1846, Virginia took back its part of the land. Some people living in DC want it to become a state, or for Maryland to take back its land, so that they can have the <a href="/wiki/Right_to_vote" class="mw-redirect" title="Right to vote">right to vote</a> in Congress. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Territories_and_possessions">Territories and possessions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=16" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Territories and possessions">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Change section: Territories and possessions">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The United States consists of sixteen lands that are not states, many of which are <a href="/wiki/Colony" title="Colony">colonial</a> <a href="/wiki/Territory" title="Territory">territories</a>. None of them have any land <a href="/wiki/Border" title="Border">borders</a> with the rest of the US. People live in five of these places, which are <i><a href="/wiki/De_facto" title="De facto">de facto</a></i> American: </p> 
      <ul>
       <li><a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/American_Samoa" title="American Samoa">American Samoa</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Guam" title="Guam">Guam</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/U.S._Virgin_Islands" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. Virgin Islands">U.S. Virgin Islands</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Northern_Mariana_Islands" title="Northern Mariana Islands">Northern Mariana Islands</a></li>
      </ul> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a> was a <a href="/wiki/Possession" title="Possession">possession</a> of the United States. <a href="/wiki/Palau" title="Palau">Palau</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Federated_States_of_Micronesia" title="Federated States of Micronesia">Federated States of Micronesia</a>, and other <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Islands" title="Pacific Islands">Pacific island</a> nations were governed by the United States as a United Nations "Trust Territory". All of these places have become <a href="/wiki/Independence" title="Independence">independent</a>: the Philippines in 1946, Palau in 1947, and Micronesia in 1986. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/U.S._armed_forces" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. armed forces">U.S. armed forces</a> has <a href="/wiki/Military_base" title="Military base">bases</a> in many countries, and the <a href="/wiki/U.S._Navy" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. Navy">U.S. Navy</a>'s base at <a href="/wiki/Guantanamo_Bay" class="mw-redirect" title="Guantanamo Bay">Guantanamo Bay</a> was rented from <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a> after that country had a <a href="/wiki/Communist" class="mw-redirect" title="Communist">Communist</a> revolution. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Counties_and_cities">Counties and cities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=17" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Counties and cities">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Change section: Counties and cities">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_United_States_cities_by_population" title="List of United States cities by population">List of United States cities by population</a>
      </div> 
      <p>All the states are divided into <a href="/wiki/Administrative_division" title="Administrative division">administrative subdivisions</a>. Most of them are called <a href="/wiki/County" title="County">counties</a>, but <a href="/wiki/Louisiana" title="Louisiana">Louisiana</a> uses the word "<a href="/wiki/List_of_parishes_in_Louisiana" title="List of parishes in Louisiana">parish</a>," and <a href="/wiki/Alaska" title="Alaska">Alaska</a> uses the word "<a href="/wiki/Borough" title="Borough">borough</a>." </p>
      <p>There are many <a href="/wiki/City" title="City">cities</a> in the United States. One city in each state is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._state_capitals" title="List of U.S. state capitals">state capital</a>, where the government of the state meets and the <a href="/wiki/Governor" title="Governor">governor</a> works. This city is not always the largest in its state. For example, the city with the most people living in it is <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a> in <a href="/wiki/New_York_(state)" title="New York (state)">New York State</a>, but the state capital is <a href="/wiki/Albany,_New_York" title="Albany, New York">Albany</a>. Some other big cities are <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles" title="Los Angeles">Los Angeles</a>, <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a>; <a href="/wiki/Chicago" title="Chicago">Chicago</a>, <a href="/wiki/Illinois" title="Illinois">Illinois</a>; <a href="/wiki/Seattle" title="Seattle">Seattle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Washington_(state)" title="Washington (state)">Washington</a>; <a href="/wiki/Miami" title="Miami">Miami</a>, <a href="/wiki/Florida" title="Florida">Florida</a>; <a href="/wiki/Indianapolis" title="Indianapolis">Indianapolis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indiana" title="Indiana">Indiana</a>; <a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas" title="Las Vegas">Las Vegas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nevada" title="Nevada">Nevada</a>; <a href="/wiki/Houston" title="Houston">Houston</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dallas" title="Dallas">Dallas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Texas" title="Texas">Texas</a>; <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia" title="Philadelphia">Philadelphia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh" title="Pittsburgh">Pittsburgh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania" title="Pennsylvania">Pennsylvania</a>; <a href="/wiki/Boston" title="Boston">Boston</a>, <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts" title="Massachusetts">Massachusetts</a>; <a href="/wiki/Denver" title="Denver">Denver</a>, <a href="/wiki/Colorado" title="Colorado">Colorado</a>; <a href="/wiki/St._Louis" title="St. Louis">St. Louis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Missouri" title="Missouri">Missouri</a>, <a href="/wiki/Memphis,_Tennessee" title="Memphis, Tennessee">Memphis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tennessee" title="Tennessee">Tennessee</a>, <a href="/wiki/Atlanta" title="Atlanta">Atlanta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(U.S._state)" title="Georgia (U.S. state)">Georgia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Detroit" title="Detroit">Detroit, Michigan</a>. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations_and_military">Foreign relations and military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=18" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Foreign relations and military">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Change section: Foreign relations and military">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_policy_of_the_United_States" title="Foreign policy of the United States">Foreign policy of the United States</a> and <a href="/wiki/Military_of_the_United_States" title="Military of the United States">Military of the United States</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Hague_Clinton_May_14_2010_Crop.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Hague_Clinton_May_14_2010_Crop.jpeg/250px-Hague_Clinton_May_14_2010_Crop.jpeg" decoding="async" width="250" height="178" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Hague_Clinton_May_14_2010_Crop.jpeg/375px-Hague_Clinton_May_14_2010_Crop.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/80/Hague_Clinton_May_14_2010_Crop.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="442" data-file-height="314"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Hague_Clinton_May_14_2010_Crop.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>British Foreign Secretary <a href="/wiki/William_Hague" title="William Hague">William Hague</a> and <a href="/wiki/U.S._Secretary_of_State" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. Secretary of State">U.S. Secretary of State</a> <a href="/wiki/Hillary_Clinton" title="Hillary Clinton">Hillary Clinton</a>, May 2010
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The United States is very influential in global economics, politics, and the military. It is a permanent member of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council" title="United Nations Security Council">United Nations Security Council</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Headquarters_of_the_United_Nations" title="Headquarters of the United Nations">headquarters of the United Nations</a> is in New York City. It is a member of the <a href="/wiki/G7" class="mw-redirect" title="G7">G7</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[58]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/G20" title="G20">G20</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Organisation_for_Economic_Co-operation_and_Development" class="mw-redirect" title="Organisation for Economic Co-operation and Development">Organisation for Economic Co-operation and Development</a>. Almost all countries have <a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_diplomatic_missions_in_the_United_States&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="List of diplomatic missions in the United States (not yet started)">embassies</a> in Washington, D.C., and many have <a href="/w/index.php?title=Consul_(representative)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Consul (representative) (not yet started)">consulates</a> around the country. Likewise, nearly all nations host <a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_diplomatic_missions_of_the_United_States&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="List of diplomatic missions of the United States (not yet started)">American diplomatic missions</a>. However, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Iran%E2%80%93United_States_relations&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Iran–United States relations (not yet started)">Iran</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=North_Korea%E2%80%93United_States_relations&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="North Korea–United States relations (not yet started)">North Korea</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Foreign_relations_of_Bhutan&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Foreign relations of Bhutan (not yet started)">Bhutan</a>, and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Taiwan%E2%80%93United_States_relations&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Taiwan–United States relations (not yet started)">Taiwan</a> do not have formal diplomatic relations with the United States. The United States has a "<a href="/w/index.php?title=Special_relationship&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Special relationship (not yet started)">special relationship</a>" with the <a href="/w/index.php?title=United_Kingdom%E2%80%93United_States_relations&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="United Kingdom–United States relations (not yet started)">United Kingdom</a><sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[59]</a></sup> and strong ties with <a href="/w/index.php?title=Canada%E2%80%93United_States_relations&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Canada–United States relations (not yet started)">Canada</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[60]</a></sup> <a href="/w/index.php?title=Australia%E2%80%93United_States_relations&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Australia–United States relations (not yet started)">Australia</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[61]</a></sup> <a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Zealand%E2%80%93United_States_relations&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="New Zealand–United States relations (not yet started)">New Zealand</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[62]</a></sup> <a href="/w/index.php?title=Japan%E2%80%93United_States_relations&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Japan–United States relations (not yet started)">Japan</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[63]</a></sup> <a href="/w/index.php?title=South_Korea%E2%80%93United_States_relations&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="South Korea–United States relations (not yet started)">South Korea</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[64]</a></sup> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Israel%E2%80%93United_States_relations&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Israel–United States relations (not yet started)">Israel</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[65]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:USS_Abraham_Lincoln_(CVN-72)_underway_in_the_South_China_Sea_on_8_May_2006_(060508-N-4166B-030).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/USS_Abraham_Lincoln_%28CVN-72%29_underway_in_the_South_China_Sea_on_8_May_2006_%28060508-N-4166B-030%29.jpg/250px-USS_Abraham_Lincoln_%28CVN-72%29_underway_in_the_South_China_Sea_on_8_May_2006_%28060508-N-4166B-030%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="166" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/USS_Abraham_Lincoln_%28CVN-72%29_underway_in_the_South_China_Sea_on_8_May_2006_%28060508-N-4166B-030%29.jpg/375px-USS_Abraham_Lincoln_%28CVN-72%29_underway_in_the_South_China_Sea_on_8_May_2006_%28060508-N-4166B-030%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/USS_Abraham_Lincoln_%28CVN-72%29_underway_in_the_South_China_Sea_on_8_May_2006_%28060508-N-4166B-030%29.jpg/500px-USS_Abraham_Lincoln_%28CVN-72%29_underway_in_the_South_China_Sea_on_8_May_2006_%28060508-N-4166B-030%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2100" data-file-height="1395"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:USS_Abraham_Lincoln_(CVN-72)_underway_in_the_South_China_Sea_on_8_May_2006_(060508-N-4166B-030).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/USS_Abraham_Lincoln_(CVN-72)" title="USS Abraham Lincoln (CVN-72)">USS <i>Abraham Lincoln</i></a> <a href="/wiki/Aircraft_carrier" title="Aircraft carrier">aircraft carrier</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The president is the <a href="https://simple.wiktionary.org/wiki/commander-in-chief" class="extiw" title="wikt:commander-in-chief">commander-in-chief</a> of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Armed_Forces" class="mw-redirect" title="United States Armed Forces">country's armed forces</a> and appoints its leaders, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Secretary_of_Defense" title="United States Secretary of Defense">secretary of defense</a> and the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Joint_Chiefs_of_Staff&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Joint Chiefs of Staff (not yet started)">Joint Chiefs of Staff</a>. The <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Defense" title="United States Department of Defense">United States Department of Defense</a> administers the armed forces, including the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Army" title="United States Army">Army</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_States_Marine_Corps" title="United States Marine Corps">Marine Corps</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_States_Navy" title="United States Navy">Navy</a>, and <a href="/wiki/United_States_Air_Force" title="United States Air Force">Air Force</a>. The <a href="/wiki/United_States_Coast_Guard" title="United States Coast Guard">Coast Guard</a> is run by the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Homeland_Security" title="United States Department of Homeland Security">Department of Homeland Security</a> in peacetime and by the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_the_Navy" title="United States Department of the Navy">Department of the Navy</a> during times of war. In 2008, the armed forces had 1.4 million personnel on active duty, along with several hundred thousand each in the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Reserve_components_of_the_United_States_Armed_Forces&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Reserve components of the United States Armed Forces (not yet started)">Reserves</a> and <a href="/wiki/National_Guard_of_the_United_States" class="mw-redirect" title="National Guard of the United States">National Guard</a> for a total of 2.3 million troops. The Department of Defense also employed about 700,000 civilians, not including contractors.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[66]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/w/index.php?title=Military_budget_of_the_United_States&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Military budget of the United States (not yet started)">military budget of the United States</a> in 2011 was more than $700 billion, 41% of global military spending and equal to the next 14 largest national military expenditures combined. At 4.7% of GDP, the rate was the second-highest among the top 15 military spenders, after <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">Saudi Arabia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[67]</a></sup> U.S. defense spending as a percentage of GDP ranked 23rd globally in 2012 according to the CIA.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[68]</a></sup> The proposed base <a href="/w/index.php?title=Military_budget_of_the_United_States&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Military budget of the United States (not yet started)">Department of Defense budget</a> for 2012, $553 billion, was a 4.2% increase over 2011; an additional $118 billion was proposed for the military campaigns in Iraq and Afghanistan.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[69]</a></sup> The last American troops serving in Iraq departed in December 2011;<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[70]</a></sup> 4,484 service members were killed during the <a href="/wiki/Iraq_War" title="Iraq War">Iraq War</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[71]</a></sup> Approximately 90,000 U.S. troops were serving in Afghanistan in April 2012;<sup id="cite_ref-Frontline_Turning_Point_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Frontline_Turning_Point-75">[72]</a></sup> by November 8, 2013 2,285 had been killed during the <a href="/wiki/War_in_Afghanistan_(2001%E2%80%93present)" title="War in Afghanistan (2001–present)">War in Afghanistan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[73]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=19" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Economy">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Change section: Economy">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>The United States has a <a href="/wiki/Capitalist" class="mw-redirect" title="Capitalist">capitalist</a> <a href="/wiki/Economy" title="Economy">economy</a>. The country has rich <a href="/wiki/Mineral" title="Mineral">mineral</a> <a href="/wiki/Natural_resource" title="Natural resource">resources</a>, with many <a href="/wiki/Gold" title="Gold">gold</a>, <a href="/wiki/Coal" title="Coal">coal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Uranium" title="Uranium">uranium</a> deposits. <a href="/wiki/Farming" title="Farming">Farming</a> makes the country among the top producers of, among others, <a href="/wiki/Corn" class="mw-redirect" title="Corn">corn</a> (<a href="/wiki/Maize" title="Maize">maize</a>), <a href="/wiki/Wheat" title="Wheat">wheat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sugar" title="Sugar">sugar</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tobacco" title="Tobacco">tobacco</a>. Housing contributes about 15% to the <a href="/wiki/Gross_Domestic_Product" class="mw-redirect" title="Gross Domestic Product">Gross Domestic Product</a> (GDP) of the United States<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[74]</a></sup> America produces <a href="/wiki/Automobile" title="Automobile">cars</a>, <a href="/wiki/Airplane" class="mw-redirect" title="Airplane">airplanes</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Electronics" title="Electronics">electronics</a>. About 3/4 of Americans work in the <a href="/wiki/Service_industry" class="mw-redirect" title="Service industry">service industry</a>. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=20" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Demographics">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Change section: Demographics">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

      <p>The United States of America has people of many different <a href="/wiki/Race_(sociology)" title="Race (sociology)">race</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_group" title="Ethnic group">ethnic</a> backgrounds. 80% of the people in the United States <a href="https://simple.wiktionary.org/wiki/descend" class="extiw" title="wikt:descend">descend</a> from <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">European</a> <a href="/wiki/Immigration" title="Immigration">immigrants</a>. Many people are descended from <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a>, <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">England</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scotland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ireland" title="Ireland">Ireland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[75]</a></sup> 13% of the people in the United States are <a href="/wiki/African-American" class="mw-redirect" title="African-American">African-American</a>. Most of them descend from the <a href="/wiki/Slave_trade" title="Slave trade">African slaves that were brought to America</a>. <a href="/wiki/Asian" class="mw-redirect" title="Asian">Asian</a>-Americans make up only 5% of the population in America but make up a bigger portion in the west coast. For example, in <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a>, Asian-Americans make up 13% of the population of that state. <a href="/wiki/Hispanic" title="Hispanic">Hispanic</a>-Americans or people of Latin origins make up 15% of the nation. The original peoples, called <a href="/wiki/Native_American" title="Native American">Native American</a>, American Indians, or Amerindians and <a href="/wiki/Inuit" title="Inuit">Inuit</a> (<a href="/wiki/Eskimo" class="mw-redirect" title="Eskimo">Eskimos</a>) are a very small group. </p>
      <p>11% of the people in the United States are foreign born. 18% speak a language other than English at home. For people 25 and older, 80% are <a href="/wiki/High_school" title="High school">high school</a> <a href="/wiki/Graduation" title="Graduation">graduates</a> while 25% have a <a href="/wiki/Bachelor%27s_degree" title="Bachelor's degree">bachelor's degree</a> or higher. </p>
      <p>The 2000 Census counted self-reported <a href="/wiki/Ancestor" title="Ancestor">ancestry</a>. It identified 43 million German-Americans, 30.5 million Irish-Americans, 24.9 million African-Americans, 24.5 million English-Americans, and 18.4 million Mexican-Americans. </p>
      <p>The United States has the largest number of immigrants of any country in the world. The United States attracts immigrants from other countries due to the <a href="/wiki/American_Dream" title="American Dream">American Dream</a>. Most immigrants in the United States come from Mexico, <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>, <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a> and <a href="/wiki/El_Salvador" title="El Salvador">El Salvador</a>. Immigration from Africa has increased. Most African immigrants come from <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">Nigeria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ethiopia" title="Ethiopia">Ethiopia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ghana" title="Ghana">Ghana</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kenya" title="Kenya">Kenya</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[76]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Money">Money</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=21" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Money">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Change section: Money">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Social" class="mw-redirect" title="Social">social</a> <a href="/wiki/Structure" title="Structure">structure</a> of the United States has a big range. This means that some Americans are much, much richer than others. The <a href="/wiki/Average" title="Average">average</a> (<a href="/wiki/Median" title="Median">median</a>) <a href="/wiki/Income" title="Income">income</a> for an American was $37,000 a year in 2002. However, the <a href="/wiki/Wealthy" class="mw-redirect" title="Wealthy">richest</a> 1% of Americans have as much money as the <a href="/wiki/Poor" class="mw-redirect" title="Poor">poorest</a> 90%. 51% of all households have access to a <a href="/wiki/Computer" title="Computer">computer</a> and 41% had access to the <a href="/wiki/Internet" title="Internet">Internet</a> in 2000, a figure which had grown to 75% in 2004. Also, 67.9% of American families owned their homes in 2002. There are 200 million cars in the United States, two for every three Americans. The debt has grown to over $21,000,000,000,000. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=22" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Religion">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Change section: Religion">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>There are many different <a href="/wiki/Religion" title="Religion">religions</a> in the U.S. <a href="/wiki/Statistics" title="Statistics">Statistically</a>, the largest religion is <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a>, including groups such as <a href="/wiki/Catholicism" title="Catholicism">Catholicism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Protestantism" title="Protestantism">Protestantism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mormonism" title="Mormonism">Mormonism</a>. Other religions include <a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">Hinduism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Judaism" title="Judaism">Judaism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Unitarian_Universalism" title="Unitarian Universalism">Unitarian Universalism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wicca" title="Wicca">Wicca</a>, <a href="/wiki/Druidry" class="mw-redirect" title="Druidry">Druidry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Baha%27i" class="mw-redirect" title="Baha'i">Baha'i</a>, <a href="/wiki/Raelism" class="mw-redirect" title="Raelism">Raelism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zoroastrianism" title="Zoroastrianism">Zoroastrianism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Taoism" title="Taoism">Taoism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jainism" title="Jainism">Jainism</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[77]</a></sup> Religions which were founded within the United States include <a href="/wiki/Eckankar" title="Eckankar">Eckankar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Satanism" title="Satanism">Satanism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Scientology" title="Scientology">Scientology</a>. <a href="/wiki/Native_American_mythology" title="Native American mythology">Native American religions</a> have various <a href="/wiki/Animism" title="Animism">animistic</a> beliefs. </p>
      <p>The United States is one of the most <a href="/wiki/Religious" class="mw-redirect" title="Religious">religious</a> countries in the <a href="/wiki/Western_World" class="mw-redirect" title="Western World">Western World</a>, and most Americans believe in <a href="/wiki/God" title="God">God</a>. The number of Christians in the U.S. has gone down. 86.2% called themselves Christian in 1990 and 78.4% said this in 2007. The others include Judaism (2.3%), Islam (0.8%), <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhism</a> (0.7%), Hinduism (0.4%), and Unitarian Universalism (0.3%). Those who have no religion are at 16.1%. There is a large difference between those who say that they belong to a religion and those who are members of a religious body of that religion.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[78]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Doubts about the existence of a God, gods or goddesses are higher among young people.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[79]</a></sup> Among the non-religious population of the U.S., there are <a href="/wiki/Deist" class="mw-redirect" title="Deist">deists</a>, <a href="/wiki/Humanist" class="mw-redirect" title="Humanist">humanists</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ignosticism" title="Ignosticism">ignotic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Atheist" class="mw-redirect" title="Atheist">atheists</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Agnostic" class="mw-redirect" title="Agnostic">agnostics</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[80]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="***REMOVED***">Language</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=23" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Language">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Change section: Language">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_the_United_States" title="Languages of the United States">Languages of the United States</a>
      </div>

      </div>

      <p><a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a> (<a href="/wiki/American_English" title="American English">American English</a>) is the de facto <a href="/wiki/National_language" title="National language">national language</a>. Although there is no <a href="/wiki/Official_language" title="Official language">official language</a> at the federal level, some laws—such as <a href="/wiki/Citizenship_in_the_United_States#Types_of_citizenship" title="Citizenship in the United States">U.S. naturalization requirements</a>—standardize English. In 2010, about 230 million, or 80% of the population aged five years and older, spoke only English at home. <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spanish_language_in_the_United_States&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Spanish language in the United States (not yet started)">Spanish</a>, spoken by 12% of the population at home, is the second most common language and the most widely taught second language.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_84-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-84">[81]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[82]</a></sup> Some Americans advocate making English the country's official language, as it is in at least twenty-eight states. Both <a href="/wiki/Hawaiian_language" title="Hawaiian language">Hawaiian</a> and English are official languages in Hawaii by state law.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[83]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>While neither has an official language, <a href="/wiki/New_Mexico" title="New Mexico">New Mexico</a> has laws providing for the use of both English and Spanish, as <a href="/wiki/Louisiana" title="Louisiana">Louisiana</a> does for English and French.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[84]</a></sup> Other states, such as <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a>, order the publication of Spanish versions of certain government documents including court forms.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[85]</a></sup> Many jurisdictions with large numbers of non-English speakers produce government materials, especially voting information, in the most commonly spoken languages in those jurisdictions. </p>
      <p>Several insular territories grant official recognition to their native languages, along with English: <a href="/w/index.php?title=Samoan_language&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Samoan language (not yet started)">Samoan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chamorro_language" title="Chamorro language">Chamorro</a> are recognized by American Samoa and Guam, respectively; <a href="/w/index.php?title=Carolinian_language&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Carolinian language (not yet started)">Carolinian</a> and Chamorro are recognized by the Northern Mariana Islands; Spanish is an official language of Puerto Rico and is more widely spoken than English there. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=24" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Education">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Change section: Education">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_the_United_States" title="Education in the United States">Education in the United States</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Educational_attainment_in_the_United_States&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Educational attainment in the United States (not yet started)">Educational attainment in the United States</a>, and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Higher_education_in_the_United_States&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Higher education in the United States (not yet started)">Higher education in the United States</a>
      </div> 
      <p>In most states, children are required to attend school from the age of six or seven (generally, kindergarten or first grade) until they turn eighteen (generally bringing them through twelfth grade, the end of high school); some states allow students to leave school at sixteen or seventeen.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[86]</a></sup> About 12% of children are enrolled in parochial or nonsectarian private schools. Just over 2% of children are homeschooled.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[87]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=25" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Culture">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Change section: Culture">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>American <a href="/wiki/Popular_culture" title="Popular culture">popular culture</a> goes out to many places in the world. It has a large <a href="/wiki/Influence" title="Influence">influence</a> on most of the world, especially the <a href="/wiki/Western_hemisphere" title="Western hemisphere">Western</a> world. American <a href="/wiki/Music" title="Music">music</a> is heard all over the world, and American movies and <a href="/wiki/Television" title="Television">television</a> shows can be seen in most countries. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Federal_holidays">Federal holidays</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=26" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Federal holidays">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Change section: Federal holidays">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

         <td>The <a href="/wiki/Autumn" title="Autumn">autumn</a> <a href="/wiki/Harvest" title="Harvest">harvest</a>, and marks the <a href="/wiki/Tradition" class="mw-redirect" title="Tradition">traditional</a> beginning of the "holiday season" </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td>December 25 </td> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Christmas" title="Christmas">Christmas</a> </td> 
         <td>Celebrates the <a href="/wiki/Birth" title="Birth">birth</a> of <a href="/wiki/Jesus_Christ" class="mw-redirect" title="Jesus Christ">Jesus Christ</a> (non-<a href="/wiki/Christian" title="Christian">Christians</a> celebrate it as a <a href="/wiki/Winter" title="Winter">winter</a> holiday) </td>

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Flag">Flag</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=27" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Flag">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Change section: Flag">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_the_United_States.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/220px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="116" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/330px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/440px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1235" data-file-height="650"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_the_United_States.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The US Flag
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The American <a href="/wiki/Flag" title="Flag">flag</a> is made up of 50 stars on a blue background, and has 13 stripes, seven red and six white. It is one of many symbols of the United States like the <a href="/wiki/Bald_Eagle" class="mw-redirect" title="Bald Eagle">Bald Eagle</a>. The 50 stars represent the 50 states. The red stands for <a href="/wiki/Courage" title="Courage">courage</a>. The blue stands for justice. The white represents peace and cleanliness. The 13 stripes represent the <a href="/wiki/Thirteen_Colonies" title="Thirteen Colonies">13 original colonies.</a><sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[89]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=28" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Cuisine">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Change section: Cuisine">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Hamburger" title="Hamburger">Hamburger</a> is the national dish of the United States. Some foods such as <a href="/wiki/Chocolate_chip_cookie" title="Chocolate chip cookie">chocolate chip cookies</a> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Corndog&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Corndog (not yet started)">corndogs</a> were invented in the United States. The United States is home to many fast food restaurants including <a href="/wiki/McDonald%27s" title="McDonald's">McDonald's</a>. <a href="/wiki/Hot_dog" title="Hot dog">Hot dogs</a> are of German origin but are eaten in the United States. Many <a href="/wiki/Soft_drink" title="Soft drink">soft drinks</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Coca-Cola" title="Coca-Cola">Coca-Cola</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pepsi" title="Pepsi">Pepsi</a> are American. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=29" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Music">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Change section: Music">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The most popular genres in the United States are <a href="/wiki/Rock_music" title="Rock music">rock</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pop_music" title="Pop music">pop</a>, <a href="/wiki/Country_music" title="Country music">country</a>, <a href="/wiki/R%26B" class="mw-redirect" title="R&amp;B">R&amp;B</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hip_hop" title="Hip hop">hip hop</a>. Famous American musicians include <a href="/wiki/Taylor_Swift" title="Taylor Swift">Taylor Swift</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eminem" title="Eminem">Eminem</a>, <a href="/wiki/Beyonc%C3%A9" title="Beyoncé">Beyoncé</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mariah_Carey" title="Mariah Carey">Mariah Carey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Britney_Spears" title="Britney Spears">Britney Spears</a>, <a href="/wiki/Katy_Perry" title="Katy Perry">Katy Perry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Madonna_(entertainer)" title="Madonna (entertainer)">Madonna</a>, <a href="/wiki/Miley_Cyrus" title="Miley Cyrus">Miley Cyrus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lil_Wayne" title="Lil Wayne">Lil Wayne</a>, <a href="/wiki/Snoop_Dogg" title="Snoop Dogg">Snoop Dogg</a> and more. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=30" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Notes">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Change section: Notes">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: lower-alpha;"> 
       <div class="mw-references-wrap">
        <ol class="references"> 
         <li id="cite_note-3"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><a href="#cite_ref-3">↑</a></span> <span class="reference-text">English is the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Official_language_of_the_United_States&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Official language of the United States (not yet started)">official language</a> of 32 states; English and <a href="/wiki/Hawaiian_language" title="Hawaiian language">Hawaiian</a> are both official languages in <a href="/wiki/Hawaii" title="Hawaii">Hawaii</a>, and English and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Alaska_Native_languages&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Alaska Native languages (not yet started)">20 Indigenous languages</a> are official in <a href="/wiki/Alaska" title="Alaska">Alaska</a>. <a href="/wiki/Algonquian_languages" title="Algonquian languages">Algonquian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cherokee_language" title="Cherokee language">Cherokee</a>, and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Sioux_language&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Sioux language (not yet started)">Sioux</a> are among many other official languages in Native-controlled lands throughout the country. <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a> is a <i>de facto</i>, but unofficial, language in <a href="/wiki/Maine" title="Maine">Maine</a> and <a href="/wiki/Louisiana" title="Louisiana">Louisiana</a>, while <a href="/wiki/New_Mexico" title="New Mexico">New Mexico</a> law grants <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a> a special status. In five territories, English as well as one or more indigenous languages are official: <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a> in Puerto Rico, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Samoan_language&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Samoan language (not yet started)">Samoan</a> in American Samoa, <a href="/wiki/Chamorro_language" title="Chamorro language">Chamorro</a> in both Guam and the Northern Mariana Islands. <a href="/w/index.php?title=Carolinian_language&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Carolinian language (not yet started)">Carolinian</a> is also an official language in the Northern Mariana Islands.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECobarrubias1983195_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECobarrubias1983195-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGarcía2011167_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGarcía2011167-2">[2]</a></sup></span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-demonym-5"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><a href="#cite_ref-demonym_5-0">↑</a></span> <span class="reference-text">The historical and informal demonym <a href="/wiki/Yankee" title="Yankee">Yankee</a> has been applied to Americans, New Englanders, or northeasterners since the 18th century.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-7"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><a href="#cite_ref-7">↑</a></span> <span class="reference-text">Also <a href="/wiki/Vice_President_of_the_United_States#Preside_over_the_United_States_Senate" title="Vice President of the United States">president of the Senate</a>.</span> </li> 
        </ol>
       </div>
      </div>
